dir="auto" class="body markup"><p><span>February 27, 2026.  If you only read press releases, you’d think quantum computing had already delivered its “ChatGPT moment.” Every few weeks a new record appears: more qubits, higher fidelity, better error correction codes, bigger funding rounds. And yet there is still an uncomfortable truth that many people in the industry gloss over: we do not yet have clear, independently verified evidence that a quantum computer can do something </span><strong>commercially</strong><span> useful that a classical computer can’t already do.</span></p><p>I have been, and remain a Quantum Computing optimist. I think we are in the late innings of an engineering challenge, not waiting on new physics. But optimism should not substitute for discipline. If you care about allocating capital rather than collecting qubit T‑shirts, the question is not “who has the most qubits?” but “who is on a credible path to commercial quantum advantage?”</p><div class="subscription-widget-wrap"><div class="subscription-widget show-subscribe"><div class="preamble"><p>The Quantum Leap is a reader-supported publication. To receive new posts and support my work, consider becoming a free or paid subscriber.</p></div><div data-component-name="SubscribeWidget" class="subscribe-widget"><div class="pencraft pc-display-flex pc-justifyContent-center pc-reset"><div class="container-IpPqBD"><form action="/api/v1/free?nojs=true" method="post" novalidate class="form form-M5sC90"><input type="hidden" name="first_url" value/><input type="hidden" name="first_referrer" value/><input type="hidden" name="current_url"/><input type="hidden" name="current_referrer"/><input type="hidden" name="first_session_url" value/><input type="hidden" name="first_session_referrer" value/><input type="hidden" name="referral_code"/><input type="hidden" name="source" value="subscribe-widget-preamble"/><input type="hidden" name="referring_pub_id"/><input type="hidden" name="additional_referring_pub_ids"/><div class="sideBySideWrap-vGXrwP"><div class="emailInputWrapper-QlA86j"><div class="pencraft pc-display-flex pc-minWidth-0 pc-position-relative pc-reset flex-auto-j3S2WA"><input name="email" placeholder="Type your email..." type="email" class="pencraft emailInput-OkIMeB input-y4v6N4 inputText-pV_yWb"/></div></div><button tabindex="0" type="submit" disabled class="pencraft pc-reset pencraft rightButton primary subscribe-btn button-VFSdkv buttonBase-GK1x3M"><span class="button-text ">Subscribe</span></button></div><div id="error-container"></div></form></div></div></div></div></div><p><span>I define commercial quantum advantage as: a quantum computer delivering measurable business value </span><strong>on a real‑world task</strong><span> that a classical system cannot match at similar cost and time. Breaking RSA‑2048 would certainly be dramatic, but that’s not the metric I care about here. I’d be happy with a humble 10% improvement in something like weather forecasting, supply‑chain planning, or portfolio optimization, independently verified and repeatable.</span></p><p>There are now hundreds of quantum hardware efforts worldwide. A recent Sutor Group landscape counts on the order of 80+ quantum processing unit (QPU) companies, while broader trackers like Quantum Navigator and QuantumZeitgeist tally nearly 200 quantum‑focused firms.  A handful of these companies are pulling ahead on the combination of technical progress, customers, capital and—importantly—third‑party validation. One of the more interesting developments in the past year has been DARPA’s Quantum Benchmarking Initiative (QBI), which is explicitly trying to answer a blunt question: can anyone build a “utility‑scale” quantum computer whose computational value exceeds its cost on useful problems by 2033?</p><p>Against that backdrop, here is my current, highly opinionated list of the 12 companies leading the race to commercial utility, and what to watch for in 2026.  This is not an exhaustive list, and it intentionally over‑weights companies where I see some path to scalable, manufacturable systems—not one‑off “hero experiments.” It’s a subjective view based on my 6 years closely following this space, and I welcome differing opinions, but here is my list, in ranked order.</p><ol><li><p>IonQ</p></li><li><p>IBM Quantum</p></li><li><p>Google Quantum AI</p></li><li><p>Quantinuum</p></li><li><p>IQM Quantum Computers</p></li><li><p>QuEra Computing</p></li><li><p>PsiQuantum</p></li><li><p>Rigetti COmputing</p></li><li><p>Xanadu</p></li><li><p>Mircosoft Quantum</p></li><li><p>PASQAL</p></li><li><p>Infleqtion</p></li></ol><p>Let’s drill down a bit…</p><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" fetchpriority="high" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>IonQ is a trapped‑ion quantum computing company that has aggressively repositioned itself as a full‑stack quantum platform, spanning computing, networking, sensing, and even space applications.  </p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>First Quantum Computing company to surpass 99.99% two‑qubit gate fidelities</strong><span> and algorithmic performance metrics like AQ (Algorithmic Qubits) in the 50–60+ range on its Tempo systems.</span></p></li><li><p>Executed a series of acquisitions—including Oxford Ionics, ID Quantique, Capella Space, and others—to build an integrated platform and recently announced an agreement to acquire SkyWater Technology to strengthen U.S. quantum manufacturing.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / market cap:</p><ul><li><p>Publicly traded (NYSE: IONQ), with a market capitalization of about $14B as of the writing of this post.​  They have raised nearly $3 billion in capital and recently reported GAAP revenues of $130M, making it the first pure‑play quantum company to cross that threshold.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch for in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>2026 will test whether IonQ can convert impressive revenue growth and acquisition activity into durable gross margins and defensible technical advantages, rather than one‑off deals. Investors should watch for clear, independently benchmarked application‑level wins rather than just bigger revenue guidance.</p></li></ul></li></ul><p></p><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>IBM, has arguably invested more and for longer in superconducting quantum computing than any other single organization, and it runs the largest fleet of cloud‑accessible quantum systems in the world.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><span>Introduced the Heron family of processors in 2023 (around 150 physical qubits) with significantly improved error rates—reportedly over an order of magnitude better effective performance than earlier systems. IBM’s 2026 roadmap centers on the </span><strong>Kookaburra modular processor, which in its full configuration</strong><span> </span><strong>is planned to deliver systems with just over 4,000 physical qubits </strong><span>and will be the first module that combines a quantum LDPC memory with a logical processing unit for error-corrected operation.</span></p></li><li><p><span>Published a long‑term roadmap stretching to 2033, centered on modular, fault‑tolerant systems and “quantum‑centric supercomputing” that tightly couples classical and quantum resources.</span><strong>  They continue to meet or beat timing deadlines for their published roadmaps.</strong></p></li><li><p>Expanded infrastructure with a European Quantum Data Center and rolled out advanced software tools like Qiskit Code Assistant and quantum‑safe security offerings.</p></li></ul><ul><li><p>IBM has been named as a performer advancing to Stage B of QBI, where it will present a detailed R&amp;D plan and have its utility‑scale architecture scrutinized for realism and scalability.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>IBM is a large, diversified public company; quantum is funded directly from its balance sheet rather than via separate venture rounds.  The IBM Quantum Network includes hundreds of organizations, from enterprises to universities, paying for access and collaboration.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to for watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>IBM’s near‑term test is whether its modular, quantum‑centric vision translates into compelling, application‑level benchmarks that show tangible advantages on chemistry, optimization, or simulation tasks—not just better hardware specs. Investors should watch for QBI feedback, evidence of logical qubit progress, and actual customer case studies that move beyond proofs of concept.​</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Google’s quantum effort, now reinforced by its acquisition of MIT spin‑out Atlantic Quantum, continues to bet on superconducting architectures while exploring next‑generation qubit designs like fluxonium.​</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Previously demonstrated landmark quantum supremacy experiments</strong><span> </span><strong>and continues to push toward error‑corrected logical qubits</strong><span>, now leveraging Atlantic Quantum’s fluxonium-based designs for longer coherence times.​</span></p></li><li><p>Uses massive GPU clusters (e.g., more than 1,000 NVIDIA H100s) to simulate quantum systems up to around 40 qubits, refining algorithms and error‑correction schemes in tandem with hardware.​</p></li><li><p>Has invested in neutral‑atom player QuEra as part of a broader ecosystem strategy.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Like IBM, Google Quantum AI is funded through its parent (Alphabet) and does not disclose separate financing rounds; Alphabet’s balance sheet gives it deep capital to pursue long‑term bets.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>The critical question is whether Google can demonstrate robust logical qubits with low logical error rates and publish clear scaling roadmaps that go beyond supremacy‑style experiments. For investors, Google’s progress is a bellwether: if a deep‑pocketed player struggles to make error‑corrected systems practical, that raises the bar for everyone else.​</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Quantinuum, formed from the merger of Honeywell Quantum Solutions and Cambridge Quantum, is a full‑stack company built around trapped‑ion hardware, a significant software portfolio, and strong enterprise relationships.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Operates some of the highest‑performing trapped‑ion systems available via cloud, with strong benchmark results on error rates and algorithmic performance</strong><span>.</span></p></li><li><p><strong>Has demonstrated a record 48 logical qubits.</strong><span>Offers a broad software stack, including TKET for circuit optimization, InQuanto for quantum chemistry, and Quantum Origin for cryptographic key generation, creating multiple revenue pathways.</span></p></li><li><p>Selected by DARPA to advance to Stage B of the Quantum Benchmarking Initiative, where its architecture and R&amp;D plan will undergo a year‑long technical validation process.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $1.16 billion dollars, most recently at a valuation in excess of $10 billion, and has filed SEC paperwork to enable a public listing that could value it substantially higher.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Quantinuum is one of the clearest candidates to demonstrate early, domain‑specific quantum advantage in chemistry or cryptography, given its integrated stack. Watch for: credible third‑party benchmarks, revenue disclosure if and when it lists, and QBI feedback on how realistic its utility‑scale path looks.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>IQM is a European superconducting‑qubit company focused on on‑premises systems for research labs and supercomputing centers, with a strong presence in the Nordics and broader EU.​</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Recently delivered superconducting quantum processors to multiple European supercomputing centers and national labs</strong><span>, positioning IQM as a key on‑premises hardware supplier for EU‑funded quantum‑HPC pilot projects.</span></p></li><li><p>Focuses on application‑specific co‑design, tailoring system architectures for domains like climate modeling and optimization alongside partners.</p></li><li><p>Announced the Halocene product line, starting with a 150‑qubit system and scaling toward 1,000‑qubit machines by the late 2020s, explicitly designed as a platform for quantum error‑correction experiments and early fault‑tolerant prototypes.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $570 million, most recently at a $1 billion post-money valuation, positioning it as one of Europe’s best‑capitalized quantum hardware start‑ups.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>IQM’s trajectory will hinge on whether European governments continue to fund dedicated quantum hardware and whether IQM can show application‑level wins in HPC settings. Investors should watch for major system deployments, follow‑on funding, or strategic alliances with cloud providers.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>QuEra is a neutral‑atom quantum computing company leveraging arrays of cold atoms controlled by lasers, with a particular emphasis on analog and hybrid digital‑analog computation.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Operates neutral‑atom systems accessible via major clouds and has demonstrated high‑qubit‑count devices suitable for certain combinatorial optimization and simulation tasks.​</p></li><li><p>Has attracted strategic investment and collaboration from Google and others, signaling confidence in neutral‑atom approaches as a scaling path.​</p></li><li><p><strong>Has demonstrated a record 48 logical qubits.</strong></p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $277 million in venture funding, although it has not disclosed the valuation. </p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>The main question is whether QuEra can turn its impressive atom counts into practical, programmable systems that outperform classical solvers on niche problems. Watch for collaborations that move from research demos to recurring commercial workloads, and for any independent benchmarking results.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>PsiQuantum is a photonic quantum computing company pursuing an all‑in, fault‑tolerant architecture based on silicon photonics and massive error correction, aiming directly for utility‑scale systems rather than small NISQ devices.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Partnered with large foundries and infrastructure providers to manufacture photonic components and build cryogenic data‑center‑like facilities.​</p></li><li><p>Has been relatively quiet on small‑scale performance metrics, emphasizing instead the necessity of jumping straight to error‑corrected architectures with millions of physical qubits.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Has raised more than $1.4 billion in venture capital and strategic funding, making it one of the best‑funded private quantum companies in the world.</strong></p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Investors should monitor whether PsiQuantum begins to show intermediate hardware milestones—such as logical qubits or small‑scale fault‑tolerant operations—and whether independent programs like QBI endorse its scaling path as plausible rather than merely ambitious. Any large strategic equity or infrastructure deals will also be important signals.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a target="_blank" 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Rigetti is a superconducting‑qubit company that went public early via a SPAC and has since refocused on improving device performance and exploring hybrid quantum‑classical workflows.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Delivered multiple generations of superconducting QPUs accessible via cloud platforms, with a focus on calibration, noise reduction, and hybrid algorithms.​</strong></p></li><li><p>Has participated in government and defense‑related quantum programs, including multi‑year R&amp;D contracts.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / market cap:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised about $850 million through venture funding and the public listing, and has a market capitalization of $6 billion although it trades at a substantially lower market capitalization than at its peak, perhaps reflecting investor skepticism about timelines and economics.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Rigetti’s key test is survival and differentiation: can it improve device performance fast enough and win enough recurring contracts to justify staying independent? Investors should watch cash burn, contract renewals, and any signs of consolidation—either as an acquirer of smaller teams or a target itself.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Xanadu is a photonic quantum company based in Canada, known both for its hardware work and for the PennyLane software framework widely used in the quantum machine‑learning community.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Demonstrated photonic devices aimed at Gaussian boson sampling and related tasks and continues to develop gate‑based photonic architectures.​</p></li><li><p><strong>PennyLane has become an important tool for variational and machine‑learning‑style algorithms across multiple hardware backends, giving Xanadu software leverage beyond its own hardware.​</strong></p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $241 million in venture funding, including from major institutional investors and strategic partners.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Watch whether Xanadu can demonstrate scalable, programmable photonic systems and tie them to concrete machine-learning or optimization tasks with measurable advantages. Any major cloud integrations or strategic partnerships around PennyLane could also shift its position in the stack.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Microsoft almost didn’t make the list because it’s quantum effort is centered on the Azure Quantum platform, which combines access to multiple other hardware backends and an emphasis on quantum‑safe cryptography and developer tooling.  However, they have announced their Majorana 1 topological machine and have been instrumental in partnering with others, such as Quantinuum and Atom, to provide the first instances of a meaningful number of logical qubits.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Azure Quantum integrates hardware from partners including IonQ, PASQAL, Quantinuum, Rigetti and Atom Computing, offering users a range of modalities through a single cloud interface.​</p></li><li><p><strong>Microsoft has reported record high‑fidelity entanglement of 48 logical qubits with Quantinuum and 24 with Atom, signaling serious progress toward logical‑qubit platforms.</strong></p></li><li><p>Microsoft has introduced AI‑assisted chemistry tools inside Azure and updated its core cryptographic libraries with post‑quantum algorithms.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Backed directly by Microsoft’s balance sheet; quantum is one of several strategic R&amp;D efforts rather than a stand‑alone funded company.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>For investors, Microsoft Quantum is less about direct revenue and more about strategic positioning: whether Azure becomes the default “control plane” for serious quantum workloads, and whether its topological qubit research yields tangible milestones. Keep an eye on logical‑qubit demonstrations and deep integrations between AI, HPC, and quantum within Azure.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a target="_blank" processing, with a strong European footprint and growing global partnerships.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><span>Deployed neutral‑atom hardware for customers and is working closely with partners like Saudi Aramco (</span><strong>where they recently deployed a 200-qubit system</strong><span>) and others on energy and optimization use‑cases.</span></p></li><li><p>Collaborates with IBM and other ecosystem players, reflecting a strategy of interoperability rather than a purely proprietary stack.​</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised over $200 million to-date and recently announced a pending additional $237 million at a $1.2 billion valuation.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Investors should watch whether PASQAL can show real‑world optimization wins and scale its neutral‑atom systems while managing reliability and control complexity. Any additional large industrial contracts or cloud integrations will be important signals of commercial readiness.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a 1272w, https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!WsfB!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F8e33e415-3148-441c-aef7-2f14929511b6_480x140.png 1456w" sizes="100vw" loading="lazy" class="sizing-normal"/></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Infleqtion (formerly ColdQuanta) is building a portfolio around cold‑atom technology that spans quantum computing, sensing, and communications, with hardware and system integration capabilities across these domains.  </p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Their SQALE demonstrated the largest reported neutral-atom array, a 16x16 (256-site) cold-atom lattice, marking a key step toward scalable, fault-tolerant neutral-atom quantum processors</strong><span>. Developed cold‑atom platforms for timing, navigation, and RF sensing, and is advancing gate‑based cold‑atom quantum computing systems.​</span></p></li><li><p>Operates facilities in multiple geographies, including the U.S. and U.K., and participates in national quantum programs.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Had raised ​$300 million in venture funding prior to their recent reverse merger, which when combined with a PIPE, brought another $500 million in funding.  Their market capitalization is now an impressive ~$2.5 billion.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Infleqtion is an interesting hedge for investors because sensing and clocks may hit commercial utility earlier than large‑scale computing. Watch for major sensing deployments, revenue disclosure, and any milestones that tie its cold‑atom platforms into broader quantum computing roadmaps.</p></li></ul></li></ul><p><strong>Summary and Conclusion</strong></p><p>If you are allocating capital—whether as a corporate buyer, LP, or direct investor—2026 is likely to be a sorting year rather than a final verdict. Here are a few things I’m watching:</p><ul><li><p>DARPA QBI Stage B outcomes and the transition toward Stage C hardware validation. Do any architectures get a clear “this looks buildable and economically promising” signal, or do most plans get gently nudged back toward the drawing board?</p></li><li><p>The first credible “10% better than classical” stories on real workloads, ideally with independent verification. </p></li><li><p>Revenue trajectories and business models. IonQ’s move past 100 million dollars of revenue is a psychological milestone, but the bigger question is whether others can follow—and whether those revenues come from repeatable products or bespoke contracts.​</p></li><li><p>Signs of consolidation. The combination of high burn rates, long timelines, and overlapping roadmaps suggests that mergers, asset sales, or strategic takeovers are likely, especially among second‑tier hardware players.</p></li><li><p>Supply‑chain and manufacturing moves. Deals like IonQ’s planned acquisition of SkyWater hint at a transition from lab‑scale devices to industrial manufacturing, which will be essential if anyone wants millions of error‑corrected qubits.</p></li></ul><p>Most importantly, resist the temptation to chase the loudest headline. Focus on:</p><ul><li><p>independently verifiable milestones rather than self‑reported metrics,</p></li><li><p>clear, realistic roadmaps to error‑corrected systems,</p></li><li><p>evidence of paying customers who stick around,</p></li><li><p>and alignment with validation frameworks like QBI that explicitly tie performance to economic value.</p></li></ul><p><span>I remain optimistic that we will see genuine commercial quantum advantage in the very near future, likely in niche domains at first. But optimism does not mean every company on this list will succeed—or that the winners will capture all the value (or that a company excluded from this list will emerge as the leader). For now, disciplined skepticism, diversified bets, and an eye on independent validation are your best tools.  And, of course, to continue to follow </span><em>The Quantum Leap</em><span> for ongoing commentary and guidance.</span></p><div class="captioned-image-container"><figure><a target="_blank" Who is leading the pack?\",\"body_html\":\"<p>February 27, 2026.  If you only read press releases, you\u2019d think quantum computing had already delivered its \u201CChatGPT moment.\u201D Every few weeks a new record appears: more qubits, higher fidelity, better error correction codes, bigger funding rounds. And yet there is still an uncomfortable truth that many people in the industry gloss over: we do not yet have clear, independently verified evidence that a quantum computer can do something <strong>commercially</strong> useful that a classical computer can\u2019t already do.</p><p>I have been, and remain a Quantum Computing optimist. I think we are in the late innings of an engineering challenge, not waiting on new physics. But optimism should not substitute for discipline. If you care about allocating capital rather than collecting qubit T\u2011shirts, the question is not \u201Cwho has the most qubits?\u201D but \u201Cwho is on a credible path to commercial quantum advantage?\u201D</p><div class=\\\"subscription-widget-wrap-editor\\\" data-attrs=\\\"{&quot;url&quot;:&quot;https://russfein.substack.com/subscribe?&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;Subscribe&quot;,&quot;language&quot;:&quot;en&quot;}\\\" data-component-name=\\\"SubscribeWidgetToDOM\\\"><div class=\\\"subscription-widget show-subscribe\\\"><div class=\\\"preamble\\\"><p class=\\\"cta-caption\\\">The Quantum Leap is a reader-supported publication. To receive new posts and support my work, consider becoming a free or paid subscriber.</p></div><form class=\\\"subscription-widget-subscribe\\\"><input type=\\\"email\\\" class=\\\"email-input\\\" name=\\\"email\\\" placeholder=\\\"Type your email\u2026\\\" tabindex=\\\"-1\\\"><input type=\\\"submit\\\" class=\\\"button primary\\\" value=\\\"Subscribe\\\"><div class=\\\"fake-input-wrapper\\\"><div class=\\\"fake-input\\\"></div><div class=\\\"fake-button\\\"></div></div></form></div></div><p>I define commercial quantum advantage as: a quantum computer delivering measurable business value <strong>on a real\u2011world task</strong> that a classical system cannot match at similar cost and time. Breaking RSA\u20112048 would certainly be dramatic, but that\u2019s not the metric I care about here. I\u2019d be happy with a humble 10% improvement in something like weather forecasting, supply\u2011chain planning, or portfolio optimization, independently verified and repeatable.</p><p>There are now hundreds of quantum hardware efforts worldwide. A recent Sutor Group landscape counts on the order of 80+ quantum processing unit (QPU) companies, while broader trackers like Quantum Navigator and QuantumZeitgeist tally nearly 200 quantum\u2011focused firms.  A handful of these companies are pulling ahead on the combination of technical progress, customers, capital and\u2014importantly\u2014third\u2011party validation. One of the more interesting developments in the past year has been DARPA\u2019s Quantum Benchmarking Initiative (QBI), which is explicitly trying to answer a blunt question: can anyone build a \u201Cutility\u2011scale\u201D quantum computer whose computational value exceeds its cost on useful problems by 2033?</p><p>Against that backdrop, here is my current, highly opinionated list of the 12 companies leading the race to commercial utility, and what to watch for in 2026.  This is not an exhaustive list, and it intentionally over\u2011weights companies where I see some path to scalable, manufacturable systems\u2014not one\u2011off \u201Chero experiments.\u201D It\u2019s a subjective view based on my 6 years closely following this space, and I welcome differing opinions, but here is my list, in ranked order.</p><ol><li><p>IonQ</p></li><li><p>IBM Quantum</p></li><li><p>Google Quantum AI</p></li><li><p>Quantinuum</p></li><li><p>IQM Quantum Computers</p></li><li><p>QuEra Computing</p></li><li><p>PsiQuantum</p></li><li><p>Rigetti COmputing</p></li><li><p>Xanadu</p></li><li><p>Mircosoft Quantum</p></li><li><p>PASQAL</p></li><li><p>Infleqtion</p></li></ol><p>Let\u2019s drill down a bit\u2026</p><div 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" fetchpriority=\\\"high\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>IonQ is a trapped\u2011ion quantum computing company that has aggressively repositioned itself as a full\u2011stack quantum platform, spanning computing, networking, sensing, and even space applications.  </p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>First Quantum Computing company to surpass 99.99% two\u2011qubit gate fidelities</strong> and algorithmic performance metrics like AQ (Algorithmic Qubits) in the 50\u201360+ range on its Tempo systems.</p></li><li><p>Executed a series of acquisitions\u2014including Oxford Ionics, ID Quantique, Capella Space, and others\u2014to build an integrated platform and recently announced an agreement to acquire SkyWater Technology to strengthen U.S. quantum manufacturing.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / market cap:</p><ul><li><p>Publicly traded (NYSE: IONQ), with a market capitalization of about $14B as of the writing of this post.\u200B  They have raised nearly $3 billion in capital and recently reported GAAP revenues of $130M, making it the first pure\u2011play quantum company to cross that threshold.\u200B</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch for in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>2026 will test whether IonQ can convert impressive revenue growth and acquisition activity into durable gross margins and defensible technical advantages, rather than one\u2011off deals. Investors should watch for clear, independently benchmarked application\u2011level wins rather than just bigger revenue guidance.</p></li></ul></li></ul><p></p><div 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>IBM, has arguably invested more and for longer in superconducting quantum computing than any other single organization, and it runs the largest fleet of cloud\u2011accessible quantum systems in the world.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Introduced the Heron family of processors in 2023 (around 150 physical qubits) with significantly improved error rates\u2014reportedly over an order of magnitude better effective performance than earlier systems. IBM\u2019s 2026 roadmap centers on the <strong>Kookaburra modular processor, which in its full configuration</strong> <strong>is planned to deliver systems with just over 4,000 physical qubits </strong>and will be the first module that combines a quantum LDPC memory with a logical processing unit for error-corrected operation.</p></li><li><p>Published a long\u2011term roadmap stretching to 2033, centered on modular, fault\u2011tolerant systems and \u201Cquantum\u2011centric supercomputing\u201D that tightly couples classical and quantum resources.<strong>  They continue to meet or beat timing deadlines for their published roadmaps.</strong></p></li><li><p>Expanded infrastructure with a European Quantum Data Center and rolled out advanced software tools like Qiskit Code Assistant and quantum\u2011safe security offerings.</p></li></ul><ul><li><p>IBM has been named as a performer advancing to Stage B of QBI, where it will present a detailed R&amp;D plan and have its utility\u2011scale architecture scrutinized for realism and scalability.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>IBM is a large, diversified public company; quantum is funded directly from its balance sheet rather than via separate venture rounds.  The IBM Quantum Network includes hundreds of organizations, from enterprises to universities, paying for access and collaboration.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to for watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>IBM\u2019s near\u2011term test is whether its modular, quantum\u2011centric vision translates into compelling, application\u2011level benchmarks that show tangible advantages on chemistry, optimization, or simulation tasks\u2014not just better hardware specs. Investors should watch for QBI feedback, evidence of logical qubit progress, and actual customer case studies that move beyond proofs of concept.\u200B</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Google\u2019s quantum effort, now reinforced by its acquisition of MIT spin\u2011out Atlantic Quantum, continues to bet on superconducting architectures while exploring next\u2011generation qubit designs like fluxonium.\u200B</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Previously demonstrated landmark quantum supremacy experiments</strong> <strong>and continues to push toward error\u2011corrected logical qubits</strong>, now leveraging Atlantic Quantum\u2019s fluxonium-based designs for longer coherence times.\u200B</p></li><li><p>Uses massive GPU clusters (e.g., more than 1,000 NVIDIA H100s) to simulate quantum systems up to around 40 qubits, refining algorithms and error\u2011correction schemes in tandem with hardware.\u200B</p></li><li><p>Has invested in neutral\u2011atom player QuEra as part of a broader ecosystem strategy.\u200B</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Like IBM, Google Quantum AI is funded through its parent (Alphabet) and does not disclose separate financing rounds; Alphabet\u2019s balance sheet gives it deep capital to pursue long\u2011term bets.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>The critical question is whether Google can demonstrate robust logical qubits with low logical error rates and publish clear scaling roadmaps that go beyond supremacy\u2011style experiments. For investors, Google\u2019s progress is a bellwether: if a deep\u2011pocketed player struggles to make error\u2011corrected systems practical, that raises the bar for everyone else.\u200B</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class=\\\"captioned-image-container\\\"><figure><a class=\\\"image-link image2\\\" target=\\\"_blank\\\" 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Quantinuum, formed from the merger of Honeywell Quantum Solutions and Cambridge Quantum, is a full\u2011stack company built around trapped\u2011ion hardware, a significant software portfolio, and strong enterprise relationships.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Operates some of the highest\u2011performing trapped\u2011ion systems available via cloud, with strong benchmark results on error rates and algorithmic performance</strong>.</p></li><li><p><strong>Has demonstrated a record 48 logical qubits.</strong>Offers a broad software stack, including TKET for circuit optimization, InQuanto for quantum chemistry, and Quantum Origin for cryptographic key generation, creating multiple revenue pathways.</p></li><li><p>Selected by DARPA to advance to Stage B of the Quantum Benchmarking Initiative, where its architecture and R&amp;D plan will undergo a year\u2011long technical validation process.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $1.16 billion dollars, most recently at a valuation in excess of $10 billion, and has filed SEC paperwork to enable a public listing that could value it substantially higher.\u200B</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Quantinuum is one of the clearest candidates to demonstrate early, domain\u2011specific quantum advantage in chemistry or cryptography, given its integrated stack. Watch for: credible third\u2011party benchmarks, revenue disclosure if and when it lists, and QBI feedback on how realistic its utility\u2011scale path looks.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Xanadu is a photonic quantum company based in Canada, known both for its hardware work and for the PennyLane software framework widely used in the quantum machine\u2011learning community.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Demonstrated photonic devices aimed at Gaussian boson sampling and related tasks and continues to develop gate\u2011based photonic architectures.\u200B</p></li><li><p><strong>PennyLane has become an important tool for variational and machine\u2011learning\u2011style algorithms across multiple hardware backends, giving Xanadu software leverage beyond its own hardware.\u200B</strong></p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised $241 million in venture funding, including from major institutional investors and strategic partners.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Watch whether Xanadu can demonstrate scalable, programmable photonic systems and tie them to concrete machine-learning or optimization tasks with measurable advantages. Any major cloud integrations or strategic partnerships around PennyLane could also shift its position in the stack.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class=\\\"captioned-image-container\\\"><figure><a 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Microsoft almost didn\u2019t make the list because it\u2019s quantum effort is centered on the Azure Quantum platform, which combines access to multiple other hardware backends and an emphasis on quantum\u2011safe cryptography and developer tooling.  However, they have announced their Majorana 1 topological machine and have been instrumental in partnering with others, such as Quantinuum and Atom, to provide the first instances of a meaningful number of logical qubits.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Azure Quantum integrates hardware from partners including IonQ, PASQAL, Quantinuum, Rigetti and Atom Computing, offering users a range of modalities through a single cloud interface.\u200B</p></li><li><p><strong>Microsoft has reported record high\u2011fidelity entanglement of 48 logical qubits with Quantinuum and 24 with Atom, signaling serious progress toward logical\u2011qubit platforms.</strong></p></li><li><p>Microsoft has introduced AI\u2011assisted chemistry tools inside Azure and updated its core cryptographic libraries with post\u2011quantum algorithms.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Backed directly by Microsoft\u2019s balance sheet; quantum is one of several strategic R&amp;D efforts rather than a stand\u2011alone funded company.\u200B</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>For investors, Microsoft Quantum is less about direct revenue and more about strategic positioning: whether Azure becomes the default \u201Ccontrol plane\u201D for serious quantum workloads, and whether its topological qubit research yields tangible milestones. Keep an eye on logical\u2011qubit demonstrations and deep integrations between AI, HPC, and quantum within Azure.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class=\\\"captioned-image-container\\\"><figure><a French neutral\u2011atom company focusing on both analog and digital quantum processing, with a strong European footprint and growing global partnerships.</p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p>Deployed neutral\u2011atom hardware for customers and is working closely with partners like Saudi Aramco (<strong>where they recently deployed a 200-qubit system</strong>) and others on energy and optimization use\u2011cases.</p></li><li><p>Collaborates with IBM and other ecosystem players, reflecting a strategy of interoperability rather than a purely proprietary stack.\u200B</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Has raised over $200 million to-date and recently announced a pending additional $237 million at a $1.2 billion valuation.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Investors should watch whether PASQAL can show real\u2011world optimization wins and scale its neutral\u2011atom systems while managing reliability and control complexity. Any additional large industrial contracts or cloud integrations will be important signals of commercial readiness.</p></li></ul></li></ul><div class=\\\"captioned-image-container\\\"><figure><a https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!WsfB!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F8e33e415-3148-441c-aef7-2f14929511b6_480x140.png 1456w\\\" sizes=\\\"100vw\\\" loading=\\\"lazy\\\"></picture><div></div></div></a></figure></div><p>Infleqtion (formerly ColdQuanta) is building a portfolio around cold\u2011atom technology that spans quantum computing, sensing, and communications, with hardware and system integration capabilities across these domains.  </p><ul><li><p>Key milestones:</p><ul><li><p><strong>Their SQALE demonstrated the largest reported neutral-atom array, a 16x16 (256-site) cold-atom lattice, marking a key step toward scalable, fault-tolerant neutral-atom quantum processors</strong>. Developed cold\u2011atom platforms for timing, navigation, and RF sensing, and is advancing gate\u2011based cold\u2011atom quantum computing systems.\u200B</p></li><li><p>Operates facilities in multiple geographies, including the U.S. and U.K., and participates in national quantum programs.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>Funds raised / valuation:</p><ul><li><p>Had raised \u200B$300 million in venture funding prior to their recent reverse merger, which when combined with a PIPE, brought another $500 million in funding.  Their market capitalization is now an impressive ~$2.5 billion.</p></li></ul></li><li><p>What to watch in 2026:</p><ul><li><p>Infleqtion is an interesting hedge for investors because sensing and clocks may hit commercial utility earlier than large\u2011scale computing. Watch for major sensing deployments, revenue disclosure, and any milestones that tie its cold\u2011atom platforms into broader quantum computing roadmaps.</p></li></ul></li></ul><p><strong>Summary and Conclusion</strong></p><p>If you are allocating capital\u2014whether as a corporate buyer, LP, or direct investor\u20142026 is likely to be a sorting year rather than a final verdict. Here are a few things I\u2019m watching:</p><ul><li><p>DARPA QBI Stage B outcomes and the transition toward Stage C hardware validation. Do any architectures get a clear \u201Cthis looks buildable and economically promising\u201D signal, or do most plans get gently nudged back toward the drawing board?</p></li><li><p>The first credible \u201C10% better than classical\u201D stories on real workloads, ideally with independent verification. </p></li><li><p>Revenue trajectories and business models. IonQ\u2019s move past 100 million dollars of revenue is a psychological milestone, but the bigger question is whether others can follow\u2014and whether those revenues come from repeatable products or bespoke contracts.\u200B</p></li><li><p>Signs of consolidation. The combination of high burn rates, long timelines, and overlapping roadmaps suggests that mergers, asset sales, or strategic takeovers are likely, especially among second\u2011tier hardware players.</p></li><li><p>Supply\u2011chain and manufacturing moves. Deals like IonQ\u2019s planned acquisition of SkyWater hint at a transition from lab\u2011scale devices to industrial manufacturing, which will be essential if anyone wants millions of error\u2011corrected qubits.</p></li></ul><p>Most importantly, resist the temptation to chase the loudest headline. Focus on:</p><ul><li><p>independently verifiable milestones rather than self\u2011reported metrics,</p></li><li><p>clear, realistic roadmaps to error\u2011corrected systems,</p></li><li><p>evidence of paying customers who stick around,</p></li><li><p>and alignment with validation frameworks like QBI that explicitly tie performance to economic value.</p></li></ul><p>I remain optimistic that we will see genuine commercial quantum advantage in the very near future, likely in niche domains at first. But optimism does not mean every company on this list will succeed\u2014or that the winners will capture all the value (or that a company excluded from this list will emerge as the leader). For now, disciplined skepticism, diversified bets, and an eye on independent validation are your best tools.  And, of course, to continue to follow <em>The Quantum Leap</em> for ongoing commentary and guidance.</p><div class=\\\"captioned-image-container\\\"><figure><a class=\\\"image-link image2
